Minor bump (1.8.2 → 1.9.0) — architectural change to date/time handling; admin-facing behavior change (kickoff times no longer skew). v1.8.2 — **Drop `revalidatePath('/')` + `revalidateTag('public-data')` from `/api/assign-player` POST + DELETE; route the player-existence check through a new lighter `getPlayerByPublicId` helper that skips the RSVP merge.** Two perf wins on the assign-player synchronous critical path. **(1) Public-data revalidation drop:** the v1.8.0 route called `revalidatePath('/') + revalidateTag('public-data', { expire: 0 })` on every link / unlink, which forced the next `/` render to re-derive the entire `LeagueData` blob from Prisma + the RSVP fanout. v1.8.1 perf measurement on a dev preview (line-mock auth) confirmed the bust is wasted work — `lineId`-derived data is NOT in the static cache (audit: `dbToPublicLeagueData.ts` doesn't read `lineId`; `linkedPlayers.ts#getLinkedPlayerIds` is uncached and called directly from `/assign-player/page.tsx`; `data.ts`/`sheets.ts`/`stats.ts` don't reference `lineId`). The link state lives in the JWT (refreshed via `next-auth#update()` on the client) and Redis (`playerMappingStore`, the canonical store consulted by the JWT callback's `getPlayerMapping`). Mirror of v1.7.0's same drop on `/api/rsvp` for the same reason. Picture-mirror revalidation kept inline — `pictureUrl` IS in the static cache, but the bust runs inside the deferred `uploadAndPersistLinePic` waitUntil callback (already off the response critical path; conditional on `linePictureUrl + BLOB_READ_WRITE_TOKEN`). Measured impact on dev preview pre-fix: GET `/` immediately after a link was 1068ms vs 488ms baseline (~580ms penalty per link warm; multi-second cold). **(2) Lighter player-validation read:** the v1.8.0 route called `await getPublicLeagueData()` to do `data.players.find((p) => p.id === playerId)`. `getPublicLeagueData` always runs `getRsvpData()` on the DB path — uncached, fans out 12+ parallel Upstash HGETALLs across all GameWeeks. Load-bearing for dashboard renders, pure overhead for write-path validation. v1.8.2 routes the validation through `lib/publicData.ts#getPlayerByPublicId(publicPlayerId)` that calls the cached `getFromDb()` / `getFromSheets()` directly and returns `{ id, name, teamId } | null` from the in-memory `players` array — no RSVP fanout. Tests: 4 new cases in `tests/unit/assignPlayerWriteInversion.test.ts` (POST does not call `revalidatePath`; POST does not call `revalidateTag` on the synchronous response path — picture-mirror revalidate is gated by `linePictureUrl + BLOB_READ_WRITE_TOKEN` which the default fixture omits; DELETE does not call either; route uses `getPlayerByPublicId('test-player')`, not `getPublicLeagueData`). `tests/unit/assignPlayerCachePrewarm.test.ts` and `tests/unit/assignPlayerBackgroundPic.test.ts` updated for the renamed mock. Patch bump (1.8.1 → 1.8.2) — perf optimization on existing contracts; no new feature, no breaking change. v1.8.1 — Operational + docs follow-up to v1.8.0 (PR 72): backfilled the PR 20 ledger row (merge `42c6e75`, prod `https://t9l-website-e14dgxslu-t9l-app.vercel.app`) + post-deploy ops-events entry capturing the Vercel preview Neon-Vercel race + admin-merge fallback + post-deploy 401-path timing samples (cold 2.13s / warm 0.51–1.09s; sanity-check only — 401 paths short-circuit before reaching the inverted code so they're a "no regression" floor, not a measurement of the architectural payoff). v1.8.0 — **Public-write hot paths invert: Redis writes block the response, Prisma writes are deferred via `waitUntil`.** Mirror of the v1.5.0 (auth) and v1.7.0 (RSVP) read-path inversions, applied to writes. Pre-fix the assign-player and RSVP POST handlers awaited Prisma on the response critical path — `prisma.$transaction` (~1–3s on cold Neon) plus cold-lambda overhead added up to the 5s post-link / RSVP delay the user reported. v1.8.0 inverts: the canonical Redis write blocks the response; the Prisma transaction runs in `waitUntil` after the response returns. Affected sites: `src/app/api/assign-player/route.ts` POST + DELETE, `src/app/api/rsvp/route.ts` POST. Skip-list (deliberate): `src/app/admin/leagues/actions.ts#adminLinkLineToPlayer`, `src/app/admin/actions.ts#updatePlayer/createPlayer/createGameWeek/deleteGameWeek` — admin pages re-read Prisma directly via `revalidatePath('/admin/...')`, so deferring Prisma there would surface stale state on the admin's own next render. Hot-path savings are public-only. **Throwing-variant adds:** `src/lib/playerMappingStore.ts#setMappingOrThrow` and `src/lib/rsvpStore.ts#setRsvpOrThrow`. Identical write shape to the silent variants but propagate Redis errors instead of swallowing them. Used only on v1.8.0 public hot paths — admin write sites continue to use the silent `setMapping`/`setRsvp` because Prisma is still the durable write target there and a Redis swallow is non-fatal. No-client (KV env unset) stays silent in both variants — that's a dev/test condition, not a prod failure mode. **Race-window tradeoff:** PR 15's `linkedPlayers` picker filter reads `Player.lineId` from Prisma, so during the deferred-write window (~1–2s waitUntil settle) a second user can see a just-claimed player as available, click Confirm, and end up with a phantom Redis mapping that gets overwritten when their own deferred Prisma write lands. Their session keeps showing them as the wrong player until the 24h sliding TTL expires or they re-link. This race already existed pre-v1.8.0 (the Prisma transaction window was ~50ms but non-zero); the window just widens. Acceptable because PR 15's filter has always been best-effort UX, not a correctness gate. **Drift recovery:** two layers. (1) Inline structured log on deferred Prisma failure: `console.error('[v1.8.0 DRIFT] kind=playerMapping op=link lineId=%s ...')` and `console.error('[v1.8.0 DRIFT] kind=rsvp gw=%s player=%s rsvp=%s ...')` — operators grep Vercel logs and replay manually. (2) New script `scripts/auditRedisVsPrisma.ts` — the inverse direction of the existing `backfillRedis<X>FromPrisma` scripts. Scans Redis (`t9l:auth:map:*` and `t9l:rsvp:gw:*`) and reports per-row state present in Redis but missing-or-differing in Prisma. `--dry-run` (default) reports a punch list; `--repair-prisma` writes the missing rows back to Prisma using Redis as truth. Two domains in one script (`--domain=playerMapping|rsvp|both`), pure decision helpers (`decidePlayerMappingAudit`, `decideRsvpAudit`) exported and unit-tested in `tests/unit/auditRedisVsPrisma.test.ts` (18 cases). **`sheets-only` writeMode unchanged** — the legacy synchronous Sheets-canonical path stays in place; v1.8.0 only inverts the `dual` and `db-only` write modes (where Redis is canonical for reads as of v1.7.0). Tests: `tests/unit/assignPlayerWriteInversion.test.ts` (7 cases — call ordering, response-before-Prisma timing via stalled-promise harness, DRIFT log on Prisma rejection, 500 on Redis throw); `tests/unit/rsvpRouteWriteInversion.test.ts` (6 cases — same shape, plus sheets-only mode keeps the synchronous path); `tests/unit/auditRedisVsPrisma.test.ts` (18 cases — pure decision helpers across match/redis-only/prisma-only/differing/malformed branches for both domains). Existing tests updated for the rename setMapping → setMappingOrThrow at the route layer: `tests/unit/assignPlayerCachePrewarm.test.ts`, `tests/unit/assignPlayerBackgroundPic.test.ts` (now asserts waitUntil called twice — once for Prisma defer, once for pic mirror), `tests/unit/rsvpRouteIntegration.test.ts` (rewritten — Prisma upsert is now INSIDE the captured-and-replayed waitUntil callback, not awaited inline). Playwright: `tests/e2e/assign-player.spec.ts` and `tests/e2e/rsvp.spec.ts` each gain a v1.8.0-specific direct-API timing test (warm POST budget <600ms — was 3–5s cold pre-v1.8.0). Minor bump (1.7.1 → 1.8.0) — architectural change to the write paths, parallel to v1.5.0 (auth) and v1.7.0 (RSVP) read-path inversions. v1.7.1 — Operational + docs follow-up to v1.7.0 (PR 19): backfilled the PR 19 ledger row + post-cutover ops-events entry. v1.7.0 — **RSVP per-matchday data migrates to Redis-as-canonical (Prisma `Availability` becomes the durable secondary).** Mirrors the v1.5.0 inversion of the lineId→Player auth path. Pre-v1.7.0 the public dashboard read RSVP via `dbToPublicLeagueData`'s `availability: true` Prisma include, wrapped in a 30s `unstable_cache`; every RSVP write had to bust `revalidateTag('public-data', { expire: 0 })` to surface, costing a full LeagueData re-derivation per submission. v1.7.0 splits the read path: cached static reads (teams/players/matchdays/matches/goals) keep the existing `unstable_cache` wrapper, and the live RSVP signals (rsvp + participated) come from Redis at dispatch time, merged into the same `LeagueData` shape consumers expect. New file `src/lib/rsvpStore.ts` mirrors `playerMappingStore.ts`: tri-state `getRsvpForGameWeek` (`hit`/`miss`/`error`), `setRsvp`/`setParticipated` per-write, `seedGameWeek` for createGameWeek pre-warm, `deleteGameWeek` for delete-time cleanup. Key shape `t9l:rsvp:gw:<gameWeekId>` — Redis HASH with `__seeded=1` sentinel + `<playerSlug>:rsvp` + `<playerSlug>:p` fields. Absolute TTL (EXPIREAT) anchored at `max(gw.startDate, now()) + 90 days` — never sliding, since RSVP data has a natural lifetime tied to the matchday. Miss → `lib/publicData.ts#getRsvpData` falls through to `prisma.availability.findMany` and pre-warms Redis with the result so the next render hits the store directly; error → defensive Prisma fallthrough WITHOUT write-back (don't amplify an Upstash blip into a write storm). New helper `src/lib/rsvpMerge.ts` owns the pure merge: `mapAvailability` (RsvpEntry → AvStatus, with the v1.6.x precedence rules — PLAYED wins over GOING/UNDECIDED, NOT_GOING/empty drop to null) and `mergeRsvpData` (per-GW Redis maps → team-keyed availability/availabilityStatuses/played triplet). RSVP route (`api/rsvp/route.ts`) now writes Prisma + Redis in the same try block (failure of either propagates as 500 — partial-write states must not survive), drops the `revalidateTag('public-data', { expire: 0 })` and `revalidatePath('/')` calls (RSVP no longer flows through the static cache). Admin GameWeek lifecycle (`admin/leagues/actions.ts`): `createGameWeek` pre-warms Redis with the `__seeded` sentinel via `seedGameWeek`; `deleteGameWeek` calls `deleteGameWeekFromRedis` for cleanup (orphan hashes would expire on their own at matchday + 90d, but eager DEL keeps the namespace tidy). `dbToPublicLeagueData` no longer derives availability — drops `availability: true` from the gameWeeks include and returns empty objects for the three RSVP-derived fields; the merge happens at the dispatcher. Sheets path (`getFromSheets`) is unchanged — still parses RSVP from RosterRaw cells, since the dataSource setting on prod is `'db'` and the Sheets path is legacy. New script `scripts/backfillRedisRsvpFromPrisma.ts` is the recovery procedure: per-GameWeek CREATE/MATCH/DRIFT-OVERWRITE decisions with a `--dry-run` mode; pure decision helper `decideBackfillAction` exported for unit testing. Tests: `tests/unit/rsvpStore.test.ts` (26 cases — tri-state read, sliding/absolute TTL math, sentinel handling, namespace isolation, RedisLike injection); `tests/unit/rsvpMerge.test.ts` (15 cases — mapAvailability precedence, merge correctness, defensive drops for unknown players/orphan GWs); `tests/unit/rsvpRouteIntegration.test.ts` (5 cases — Prisma upsert + setRsvp both fire, no `revalidateTag`, slug-not-prefixed-id passed to setRsvp, 500 on Prisma failure with no Redis side-effect); `tests/unit/backfillRedisRsvpFromPrisma.test.ts` (15 cases — buildTargetFields shape, decideBackfillAction CREATE/MATCH/DRIFT branches). Existing `tests/unit/dbAdapterHelpers.test.ts` lost the 6 `mapAvailability` cases (moved to rsvpMerge). New Playwright spec `tests/e2e/rsvp.spec.ts` (gated to localhost + an `E2E_LINE_ID` env var pre-linked to a roster player) submits an RSVP via the API, reloads the dashboard, and asserts the new status renders within the architectural-payoff budget. **Cutover protocol:** run `npx tsx scripts/backfillRedisRsvpFromPrisma.ts --dry-run --verbose` against prod Upstash BEFORE merging, surface output for sign-off, run `--apply` to seed prod Redis, THEN merge. Otherwise the first dashboard render post-deploy hits miss for every GW and falls through to Prisma simultaneously — transient cold-Neon storm. Out of scope for v1.7.0: Sheets dual-write retirement (still fires Sheets writes in `dual` mode); admin-write of `participated` (no admin endpoint writes it today). Minor bump (1.6.1 → 1.7.0) — architectural change to the RSVP read path. v1.6.1 — **`/assign-player` Confirm fires `router.push('/')` SYNCHRONOUSLY on click; the API write runs in the background; the Sonner toast confirms outcome on the destination.** v1.6.0 (PR 17) shipped the auto-navigate + toast UX but awaited `attemptLink` BEFORE firing `router.push('/')`. On a cold Vercel lambda the API write is 3–5s, so the user clicked Confirm, watched the button stuck on "Saving…" for 3–5s, and only saw the toast appear when the route finally changed — which read as "navigation tied to toast dismissal" because nothing happened until the toast did. v1.6.1 (PR 18) inverts the order via a new pure helper `src/lib/assignSubmit.ts` (`performAssignSubmit`): step 1 `pushHome()` synchronously, step 2 `await link(playerId)` (background from the user's POV — they've already navigated), step 3 `notifyLinkOutcome(result, toast)` (toast on the destination), step 4 fire-and-forget `refreshSession()` on success, step 5 `onError(err)` on failure. The component (`AssignPlayerClient.tsx`) wraps `pushHome` in `startTransition(() => router.push('/'))` and wires `refreshSession` to next-auth's `update()`. Error path: the user has already navigated to `/`; the error toast is the surface, and a manual return to `/assign-player` is acceptable since the picker filters linked players server-side (PR 15) so the only realistic failure is a 5xx. Vitest in `tests/unit/assignSubmit.test.ts` pins 6 cases — the regression target is "calls pushHome BEFORE the link API resolves" via a deferred-promise ordering harness that drains microtasks between push and link-resolve; a regression to v1.6.0's await-then-push order would fail this test. Playwright spec rewritten again: case 1 click→nav budget tightened from 5s to 1.5s (the v1.6.0 spec was too lax — it would have passed even on cold lambdas, which is what let this regression ship); case 2 inverted — the 2s API stall now asserts the user lands on `/` BEFORE the stall ends (i.e. nav fires synchronously), with the toast appearing post-navigation once the write completes. Patch bump (1.6.0 → 1.6.1) — bug fix, no contract change. v1.6.0 — **`/assign-player` auto-navigates to `/` on link success; toast confirms via global Sonner provider in root layout.** v1.4.0 (PR 13) replaced the auto-navigate with an inline "✓ Linked to {Player Name}" success view + an explicit Go-home button — that closed the cold-Vercel-lambda perceived-latency story for the optimistic flip but added a friction step (the user had to click Go-home to leave). User reported it as worse, not better: the Go-home click was just a beat after the satisfaction of seeing their name appear. v1.6.0 reverses: `attemptLink` resolves → `notifyLinkOutcome(result, toast)` (success or error) → `router.push('/')` immediately on success. The toast lives at the root layout (`<Toaster />` from `sonner`), persists across the route navigation, auto-dismisses after ~4.5s, and renders the success/error message on whichever page the user is on. New helper `src/lib/assignToast.ts` is the pure dispatch boundary — `notifyLinkOutcome` / `notifyUnlinkOutcome` take a `LinkAttemptResult` / `UnlinkAttemptResult` and a minimal `ToastApi` shape (`{ success, error }`) and route to the right side; vitest pins 6 cases (success/error/empty-error fallback for both). Production callers pass sonner's `toast` directly. The inline success view + "Go to home" button + "Finalizing…" button + `apiPromiseRef` / `updatePromiseRef` await-the-pipeline state from PR 13 are all removed — the new flow doesn't need them because the user is on `/` by the time the next-auth refresh would complete (the destination uses next-auth client cache; brief stale-flash on slow refetches is the same accepted tradeoff from PR 11 / v1.3.0). `useOptimistic` is removed from `AssignPlayerClient.tsx` since there's no inline view consuming the optimistic value; `setSubmitting` now provides the in-flight feedback via `assignButtonLabel` (label flips to "Saving…" between click and navigation). `LinkedState` type export deleted from `optimisticLink.ts` (only consumer was the now-removed inline view). Playwright spec rewritten: case 1 clicks Confirm → asserts URL is `/` within 5s + a Sonner `role="status"` toast containing "Linked to {Player Name}" is visible within 2s + auto-dismisses within 8s (Sonner's 4.5s duration + exit animation slack); case 2 stalls the POST by 2s, asserts the user stays on `/assign-player` with a "Saving…" button label until the API resolves, then lands on `/` and the toast still fires post-navigation. Minor bump (1.5.0 → 1.6.0) — UX behavior change (inline success view → auto-navigate + toast). New dep: `sonner ^2.0.7`. v1.5.0 — **Architectural inversion of the lineId→Player auth lookup: Redis is now primary, Prisma is the durable secondary.** Pre-v1.5.0 the JWT callback path was `Upstash cache (60s TTL) → miss falls through to Prisma → result cached`. PRs 8/9/10/11/12 chipped at the cold-Neon-Prisma-on-JWT latency incrementally; v1.5.0 just removes the fallback. Read path is now `Redis store (24h sliding TTL) → miss returns null (orphan, no Prisma fallback) → error falls through to Prisma defensively (Upstash transient outage must not null every authenticated session)`. Every authenticated request is bounded by an Upstash REST round-trip (~50–100ms) instead of a possible cold-Neon Prisma relation-include (~1–3s). New file `src/lib/playerMappingStore.ts` (renamed from `playerMappingCache.ts`) returns a tri-state result `{ status: 'hit' | 'miss' | 'error' }` so the auth callback can apply the v1.5.0 policy correctly — the previous shape collapsed miss/error into `undefined` and made them indistinguishable. Sliding TTL: every read hit fires a fire-and-forget `expire(key, 24h)` so active users never expire; long-inactive users (no auth refresh in 24h) → key expires → next access → miss → orphan. The 24h window also serves as a self-healing safety net for write-path bugs: a forgotten `setMapping` decays within 24h instead of persisting indefinitely. Write sites (`api/assign-player` POST/DELETE, `admin/actions` updatePlayer/createPlayer, `admin/leagues/actions` adminLinkLineToPlayer) keep their existing Prisma-first-then-Redis-pre-warm order — the v1.5.0 framing changes (Redis is canonical, Prisma is durable backup that powers the admin-filter query and the recovery script) but the dual-write itself is unchanged. The legacy Redis hash fallback (`getPlayerMappingFromRedis` reading `line-player-map`, PR 6 deprecation window) is removed entirely — the v1.5.0 store reads from a different namespace (`t9l:auth:map:`) and every LINE user was migrated to `Player.lineId` by the PR 6 backfill, so there is no remaining role for the legacy hash. The defensive `legacyRedisCleanup` HDEL calls in `api/assign-player` are kept so any residual entries decay to empty. New script `scripts/backfillRedisFromPrisma.ts` is the recovery procedure: bulk-reads `Player.lineId` rows, compares against Redis, and reports per-row CREATE/MATCH/DRIFT-OVERWRITE decisions with a `--dry-run` mode for operator review and `--apply` for the actual write. Pure decision helper `decideBackfillAction` is unit-tested in `tests/unit/backfillRedisFromPrisma.test.ts` across 8 cases (missing/match/drift/auto-parsed/null-sentinel/malformed/single-field-diff). Tests: `playerMappingCache.test.ts` rewritten as `playerMappingStore.test.ts` (24 tests covering tri-state get, sliding TTL behavior, set/delete semantics, namespace isolation, no-Redis-configured fallthrough); new `getPlayerMapping.test.ts` (6 tests pinning the auth-side miss-vs-error policy via `__getPlayerMapping_for_testing`). All write-site tests updated for the renamed exports (`setCached → setMapping`, `invalidate → deleteMapping`). Recovery procedure documented in CLAUDE.md runbook section: if Upstash data loss / accidental wipe ever happens, run `npx tsx scripts/backfillRedisFromPrisma.ts --apply` to rebuild the store from Prisma. Minor bump (1.4.3 → 1.5.0) — architectural change to the auth path. The user-facing behavior is identical to v1.4.3 in steady state; the operational story (which store is canonical, what the recovery procedure looks like) is the substantive shift. v1.4.3 — Two user-reported bugs in the live link flow, both real, fixed together. **(1) `Failed to execute 'fetch' on 'Window': Illegal invocation`** on every link AND unassign click in the public site. Diagnosis: `AssignPlayerClient.tsx` was calling `attemptLink(id, { fetch })` and `attemptUnlink({ fetch })`, and the helpers in `src/lib/optimisticLink.ts` invoked `deps.fetch(...)` internally. That calls fetch as a *method of the plain `deps` object*, and the browser's WebIDL receiver brand check on `fetch` rejects any `this` that isn't a Window/Worker → "Illegal invocation". Vitest `vi.fn()` spies have no brand check, so the existing unit suite passed cleanly while every real link/unlink in production threw and rolled back the v1.4.0 optimistic flip — the user saw a flash-then-revert, not a successful link. Fix: `deps` is now optional on both helpers, and the no-deps path routes through a module-scope free-function wrapper (`(input, init) => fetch(input, init)`) which calls fetch as a global — that's the realm-bound dispatch the WebIDL spec uses for the global call form, no `this` issues. Production callers (`AssignPlayerClient.tsx`) drop `{ fetch }` from both call sites; test injection still works via the optional `{ fetch: spy }` shape (the existing optimisticLink test suite continues to pass unchanged). New regression tests in `tests/unit/optimisticLink.test.ts` pin the no-deps→global-fetch contract for both `attemptLink` and `attemptUnlink` via `vi.stubGlobal('fetch', ...)`. Caveat: vitest can't reproduce the actual brand-check throw (jsdom doesn't enforce it); the unit test pins call SHAPE (where the call originates), and the Playwright spec exercises the full path against a real browser. **(2) Hide linked players entirely** instead of greying them out (UX preference: clean picker showing only what the viewer can pick; PR 14's transparency-via-greying gave more information than the user wanted). Filter moved to the page layer in `src/app/assign-player/page.tsx`: `data.players.filter((p) => p.teamId === team.id && !linkedIds.has(p.id))` — linked players never reach the client. The `annotatePlayersWithLinkedStatus` helper and its unit test file are deleted (no longer used; `getLinkedPlayerIds` is the only export `linkedPlayers.ts` keeps). The client-side linked-row branch in `AssignPlayerClient.tsx` is deleted (linked players never render). Playwright e2e tightened: instead of asserting `data-linked="true"` + `aria-disabled="true"` + "Already linked" tag, now asserts `getByTestId(linkedSlugRow).toHaveCount(0)` — i.e. the linked player is absent from the DOM. Patch bump (1.4.2 → 1.4.3) — bug fixes, no new feature. v1.4.2 — Filter already-linked players from `/assign-player` selectable list. Pre-fix the picker rendered every roster row regardless of whether another LINE user already held that `Player.lineId` — the user could pick a claimed player, the optimistic UI from v1.4.0 would flash success, then the API would 409 and the rollback path would fire. v1.4.2 reads `Player.lineId IS NOT NULL` from Prisma at SSR time (excluding the viewer's own `lineId` so they can re-confirm or unassign their own player), passes the resulting public-slug set to a pure annotator (`annotatePlayersWithLinkedStatus` in `src/lib/linkedPlayers.ts`), and the client renders linked rows as a non-clickable `<div>` with a line-through name + `Already linked` tag at 50% opacity. The row stays visible (roster transparency) but cannot be selected — the false-success path is closed at the data layer rather than at the API. The viewer's own player remains selectable so the existing "you're linked, click again to unassign" flow on `isAlreadyAssigned` still works. New unit tests in `tests/unit/linkedPlayers.test.ts` pin the annotator across seven cases (in-set/not-in-set, empty-set, group ordering, full-field preservation, immutability, viewer-exclusion seam). New Playwright spec links a roster player as user A via the API, opens a fresh browser context as user B (distinct dev-login `lineId`), and asserts the linked row renders with `data-linked="true"`, `aria-disabled="true"`, the "Already linked" tag, and IS NOT a `<button>` — with cleanup unlinking via DELETE in a `finally` so the dev DB returns to its prior state. Patch bump (1.4.1 → 1.4.2) — UX polish that closes a false-success footgun without changing the link contract itself. **(Note:** v1.4.3 supersedes v1.4.2's behavior — see above; v1.4.2 stayed live for ~30 minutes before user reports surfaced the Illegal-invocation bug and the UX preference flip.) v1.4.1 — Docs-only follow-up to v1.4.0: backfills the PR 13 ledger row (merge `29c0f55`, prod `https://t9l-website-7968i3pbl-t9l-app.vercel.app`) into the per-PR snapshot ledger and the PR 13 status entry under [Sheets→DB migration](#sheetsdb-migration). v1.4.0 — Optimistic UI rewrite of the public assign-player flow. PRs 10/11/12 structurally cut latency from ~6s to ~3s but never made the click feel instant — the user still saw a "Saving…" → "Done — redirecting…" sequence followed by an RSC navigation. v1.4.0 makes the click perceived-instant via `useOptimistic`: the form is replaced by an inline success view ("✓ You're linked to {Player Name}" + team-color badge + "Go to home →" button) the moment the user clicks Confirm, before the API resolves. The auto-navigate to `/` is removed — the user pays the navigation cost on their own schedule. The Go-home button awaits the in-flight API write + next-auth `update()` if pressed before they settle (it briefly shows "Finalizing…"), so the destination never renders with a stale JWT — and on API failure the optimistic state reverts via `useOptimistic` end-of-transition semantics, the user stays on `/assign-player` with an error toast for retry. Helpers `lib/postAssignNavigate.ts` and `lib/kickOffSessionRefresh.ts` (both shipped in PRs 10/11) are removed because the new flow no longer auto-navigates. New unit tests in `tests/unit/optimisticLink.test.ts` pin the rollback gate (`attemptLink`/`attemptUnlink` discriminated-union return shape across 200/4xx/5xx/network-failure paths). Playwright spec tightened: success-view-visible-within-50ms-of-click target (DoD <50ms; assertion budget 150ms for CI jitter); plus a new case that stalls the API by 2s, clicks Confirm + Go-home immediately, and asserts the navigation defers until the pipeline settles. Minor bump (1.3.2 → 1.4.0) — UX behavior change. v1.3.2 (PR 12.5) — Docs-only follow-up to v1.3.1: backfilled the PR 12 ledger row (merge `9d51ed9`, prod `https://t9l-website-co1k0pqzm-t9l-app.vercel.app`) and captured the post-cutover cold/warm timing baseline against apex (unauth) — `/api/auth/session` 1.37s cold / 0.52s warm; `/` 1.82s cold / 0.99s warm; `/api/assign-player POST` (401) 1.89s cold / 0.51s warm. Each cold lambda is ~1–2s of fixed cost; the user's perceived "5–7s" assign-player hang was the sum of multiple cold round-trips serially. PRs 10/11/12 collectively remove two of them (the redundant `router.refresh()` and the awaited `update()`) plus 200–500ms of inline Blob upload, leaving the synchronous critical path at: API write (Prisma transaction + cache pre-warm + revalidate) + RSC navigation to `/`. Cold-most-of-the-time perception drops from ~5–7s to ~2–3s — but still not instant, which is what motivates v1.4.0. v1.3.1 (PR 12) — Third in the cold-lambda perceived-latency push on assign-player. Moves the LINE-profile-picture mirror (LINE-CDN fetch + Vercel Blob `put` + Redis SET + `Player.pictureUrl` update) off the API response critical path. Pre-fix the entire chain ran serially before the route returned, costing 200–500ms warm and meaningfully more cold on every assign that had a LINE picture. Now the synchronous part of the route is just the Prisma transaction (set `Player.lineId`) + cache pre-warm + revalidate; the picture work runs out of band via `waitUntil(uploadAndPersistLinePic(...))` from `@vercel/functions`. Background work calls `revalidateTag('public-data', { expire: 0 })` on success so the picture appears on the next page render instead of waiting up to 30s for `unstable_cache` to expire. Destination renders with `PlayerAvatar`'s built-in fallback chain (LINE CDN URL → `/player_pics/{name}.png` → `default.png`) until the upload completes — typically <1s in the background. Vitest in `tests/unit/assignPlayerBackgroundPic.test.ts` pins five contracts: `waitUntil` called exactly once when picture data is present, response returns 200 even when the put-Promise never resolves (the regression target — if the route awaits `put`, this test times out), Prisma transaction's `data` does NOT include `pictureUrl`, no `waitUntil` when `linePictureUrl` is empty, no `waitUntil` when `BLOB_READ_WRITE_TOKEN` is unset. Patch bump (1.3.0 → 1.3.1) — perf optimization, no semantic change to the link contract itself. Combined with PRs 10 (drop redundant `router.refresh()` + `startTransition`) and 11 (drop awaited `update()`), the assign-player critical path has lost two cold-startable round-trips and 200–500ms of inline blob work; what remains is the Prisma transaction + the cache pre-warm + revalidate calls. v1.3.0 (PR 11) prod: `https://t9l-website-36ub5hp2d-t9l-app.vercel.app`. Constant lives in `src/lib/version.ts`; bump there and update this line on each release.

> **Version-bump rule:** Every PR bumps `APP_VERSION` in `src/lib/version.ts` as part of the change.
> - Patch bump (1.1.0 → 1.1.1) — fixes, chores, refactors, docs.
> - Minor bump (1.1.0 → 1.2.0) — new user-visible features.
> - Major bump (1.1.0 → 2.0.0) — breaking changes / migrations of public contracts.
> The bump lives in the same commit as the change. The matching test in `tests/unit/version.test.ts` updates in the same commit. After merge, the autonomy post-merge sequence pushes an annotated release tag `v<APP_VERSION>` at the merge SHA — separate from the rollback tag (`v-pre-pr-N-...`).

> **Maintenance rule:** Whenever an architectural decision is made — new component, changed data flow, new API route, new Prisma model or column, modified Sheet schema, UX philosophy change — update this file **in the same PR** as the change. PRs that touch architecture without updating CLAUDE.md should be sent back. This file is the single source of truth for how the project works.
>
> **Test rule:** Every PR that adds or changes behavior ships with at least one test that proves the new behavior. Unit tests for pure functions (Vitest), e2e tests for user-visible flows (Playwright). The CI workflow at `.github/workflows/test.yml` runs Vitest + tsc on every PR; merge is blocked on red. See [Testing](#testing) below for what to add per change-type.
>
> **End-to-end verification rule:** Every PR's tests must verify the BEHAVIOR the PR claims to fix, not just that the code compiles. For perf claims, time before/after on dev preview and capture in the PR description. For UX claims, Playwright assertions on the user-visible outcome (not the implementation detail). For correctness claims, a regression test that fails on the broken state — e.g. for the v1.9.0 JST fix, a test that takes "14:30 JST" through parse → store → display and asserts the displayed time is "14:30", which would have failed on the v1.8.x V8/Vercel TZ=UTC bug. "Doesn't crash" is not verification; "produces the claimed outcome" is.
>
> **Autonomy rule:** The Claude Code harness reads `.claude/settings.json` (committed) and `.claude/settings.local.json` (gitignored, per-developer override). The committed file pre-approves routine read/edit/grep/install/test/git/gh/vercel/neonctl tools and explicitly **denies** destructive Bash patterns (`git push --force*`, `git reset --hard*`, `rm -rf*`, `prisma migrate reset*`, `neonctl branches delete*`, raw SQL `DROP/TRUNCATE/DELETE FROM`). If a routine command is hitting an approval prompt, propose adding it to `permissions.allow` in `.claude/settings.json` rather than `settings.local.json` so the whole team benefits.
>
> **Cache invalidation rule (v1.16.0):** Cache invalidation goes through [`src/lib/revalidate.ts#revalidate({ domain })`](src/lib/revalidate.ts). Direct `revalidateTag` / `revalidatePath` / `updateTag` calls outside that file are forbidden. The lint guard at [`tests/unit/revalidatePrimitivesGuard.test.ts`](tests/unit/revalidatePrimitivesGuard.test.ts) fails CI if any new primitive call leaks. Domains are `'public' | 'admin' | 'settings' | 'all'`; modes are `'action'` (default; uses `updateTag` for read-your-own-writes inside server actions) and `'route'` (uses `revalidateTag(tag, { expire: 0 })` for route handlers). Pass `paths: [...]` to add per-action `revalidatePath` busts. See the helper's docstring for the full domain → tag-set table.
>
> **Plan-then-ship autonomy rule (v1.9.0):** Plans grounded in code audit + tests that verify the planned behavior may proceed to ship without orchestrator ack. The audit-grounded plan IS the gate — once you've surfaced scope, identified the load-bearing bug, and laid out tests that would fail on the broken state, ship sequentially through the planned PR list (commit → push → admin-merge per Neon-Vercel race fallback → tag → ledger → smoke), then report the chain at the end. The dev environment is yours to instrument, deploy to, and modify for verification.
>
> **Per-push reporting rule (v1.11.2):** Plan-then-ship does NOT mean silent batched delivery. Surface a one-line status to the orchestrator at three points per PR so the user can track progress in real time:
> 1. **On `git push` of the PR branch:** `> PR #N pushed: <one-line description>. <merge state — admin-merging now / waiting for CI>. Next: <PR M or smoke step>.`
> 2. **On merge:** `> PR #N merged at <SHA>. Tag v<X.Y.Z> pushed. Waiting for prod deploy.` (or `Prod deploy clean.`)
> 3. **On prod live (apex serving the new version):** `> v<X.Y.Z> live on apex.` (one line, no elaboration)
>
> Keep each surface short — one or two sentences max. Don't elaborate beyond what the user needs to track progress. The full PR description, test counts, and verification details live in the GitHub PR body and the final-chain report; the per-push surfaces are just signal markers.
>
> **Stop conditions still apply** even under plan-then-ship autonomy: data destruction (Layer 3 / 4 / 5 / 5b / 5c rollback paths), schema irreversibility (DROP COLUMN, type changes that lose data), prod write surprise (a PR turns out to write to prod via an unexpected code path), or ambiguity that's actually a product decision (UX flow that has multiple defensible answers and the user hasn't picked one). Surface these IMMEDIATELY rather than guessing. The Neon-Vercel preview-env race is NOT a stop condition — it's the documented race in [Known infra issues](#known-infra-issues), and the runbook fallback is `gh pr merge <num> --admin --merge` once Unit + type-check is green on the PR.

## Project

T9L.me — mobile-first website for the Tennozu 9-Aside League, a recreational football league in Tokyo. Players can log in via LINE, assign themselves to their roster entry, RSVP availability for upcoming matchdays, and view live league data sourced from a Google Sheet.

## Stack

- Next.js (App Router, server + client components, ISR)
- TypeScript (strict mode)
- Tailwind CSS v4
- `googleapis` — Google Sheets API (read + write) — public-site source of truth on apex (cutover to DB in progress; see [Sheets→DB Migration](#sheetsdb-migration))
- `@prisma/client` + `@neondatabase/serverless` — Postgres ORM (Neon-hosted) — admin-side source of truth and target of public-site cutover
- `next-auth` v4 — LINE OAuth (public players) + Credentials provider (admin)
- `@upstash/redis` — Canonical store for lineId→Player mapping (v1.5.0) and per-GameWeek RSVP signals (v1.7.0). Also caches Vercel Blob URLs for player pics.
- `@vercel/blob` — Player profile picture storage (LINE-CDN mirror)
- `sonner` — Toast notifications (global Toaster mounted in app/layout.tsx)
- Vitest (unit) + Playwright (e2e) — see [Testing](#testing)
- Deployed to Vercel; Neon-Vercel marketplace integration auto-provisions a Neon branch DB per Vercel preview branch

## Architecture Overview

```
Google Sheets (source of truth)
       ↕ read (batchGet) + write (availability cell updates)
  lib/sheets.ts
       ↓ parse
  lib/data.ts → lib/stats.ts
       ↓
  app/page.tsx (server component, dynamic — reads host header)
       └─ getLeagueIdFromRequest() → getPublicLeagueData(leagueId)
              → components/Dashboard.tsx  (v1.25.0 — apex + subdomain unified)
                  ├── NextMatchdayBanner       (Home — match info + selector)
                  ├── MatchdayAvailability     (Home — per-team attendance)
                  ├── RsvpBar                  (Home — fixed-bottom RSVP)
                  ├── UserTeamBadge            (Home — "your team is X")
                  └── GuestLoginBanner         (Home — guest CTA)
       (apex / dev base / localhost / vercel preview → default league)
       (known subdomain → that league)
       (unknown subdomain → 404 surface)

  /schedule  → MatchdayCard list (subdomain-aware via getLeagueIdFromRequest)
  /stats     → LeagueTable + TopPerformers + StatsDashboard (subdomain-aware)

LINE OAuth → next-auth JWT callback → src/lib/playerMappingStore.ts (Upstash, primary)
                                       └ on store error: defensive Prisma fallback
Player link → api/assign-player → setMappingOrThrow (sync, Redis canonical)
                                  └ waitUntil(prisma.$transaction)  # v1.8.0 deferred
RSVP writes  → api/rsvp → setRsvpOrThrow (sync, Redis canonical)
                          └ waitUntil(prisma.availability.upsert)   # v1.8.0 deferred
RSVP reads   → src/lib/publicData.getRsvpData → rsvpStore (HGETALL/GW)
                                       └ on miss: Prisma fallback + Redis pre-warm
                                       └ on error: Prisma fallback (no write-back)
i18n → `googtrans` cookie set by LanguageToggle → Google Translate (no app-side translation pipeline)
Player pics → /stats reads Redis `player-pic:<slug>` → Vercel Blob URL (LINE-CDN mirror)
              Public dashboard uses PlayerAvatar's static fallback chain at render time.
```

**RSVP store (PR 19 / v1.7.0).** RSVP signals (`rsvp` + `participated`) are read from Redis on every public-dashboard render, not from Prisma. `src/lib/rsvpStore.ts` is the canonical store; `prisma.Availability` is the durable secondary that backs admin queries and the recovery script. Key shape `t9l:rsvp:gw:<gameWeekId>` — Redis HASH with `__seeded=1` sentinel + `<playerSlug>:rsvp` + `<playerSlug>:p` fields. Absolute TTL (EXPIREAT) anchored at `max(gw.startDate, now()) + 90 days` — never sliding, since RSVP data has a natural lifetime tied to the matchday. Read path: `getRsvpForGameWeek(gwId, gwStartDate)` returns a discriminated `{ status: 'hit'|'miss'|'error' }`; `lib/publicData.ts#getRsvpData` runs the batched read + applies the v1.7.0 policy: `hit` → use it (including legitimate empty-with-sentinel), `miss` → Prisma fallthrough + Redis pre-warm, `error` → Prisma fallthrough WITHOUT write-back (don't amplify Upstash blips into write storms). Write sites: `api/rsvp/route.ts` calls `setRsvp(gwId, gwStartDate, playerSlug, rsvp)` after the Prisma upsert in the same try block (failure of either propagates as 500). Admin GameWeek lifecycle: `createGameWeek` calls `seedGameWeek` to mark the hash initialized; `deleteGameWeek` calls `deleteGameWeek` (Redis) for cleanup.

**Auth/perf — Redis-primary mapping store (PR 16 / v1.5.0).** The lineId→Player lookup on every JWT callback resolves through `src/lib/playerMappingStore.ts` (Upstash, **24h sliding TTL**, `t9l:auth:map:` namespace, null sentinel for unmapped LINE IDs). **Redis is canonical, Prisma is the durable secondary.** Pre-v1.5.0 the file was named `playerMappingCache` and acted as a 60s cache-aside in front of Prisma — every miss fell through to Prisma. PR 16 inverts that: a `miss` returns `null` directly (orphan; the user must re-link), and only an `error` (Upstash unreachable) falls through to Prisma defensively so a transient outage doesn't null every authenticated session. The `getMapping` return shape is now a discriminated union `{ status: 'hit'|'miss'|'error' }` so the auth callback can distinguish these branches. The sliding TTL means active users (any auth refresh inside 24h) effectively never expire; long-inactive users → key expires → next access → orphan.

**Writes pre-warm, they do NOT delete-then-cold-read** — every site that mutates `Player.lineId` (`api/assign-player` POST/DELETE, `admin/actions.ts#updatePlayer/createPlayer`, `admin/leagues/actions.ts#adminLinkLineToPlayer`) calls `setMapping(lineId, freshMapping)` after the Prisma write, using the exported `getPlayerMappingFromDb` helper for shape parity. This is load-bearing under v1.5.0 because there's no longer a Prisma fallback in the happy-path read — a forgotten `setMapping` would silently leave the user as orphan until an admin write touches them or the 24h sliding TTL pulls them back to a fresh re-link. The OLD lineId on `updatePlayer` deliberately uses `deleteMapping` (formerly `invalidate`) — that user's mapping has just been transferred to a different player, and a fresh miss-then-orphan is the correct post-write state.

**Recovery procedure.** If Upstash ever loses data or the namespace is cleared, run `npx tsx scripts/backfillRedisFromPrisma.ts --dry-run` to see the rebuild plan, then `--apply` to actually rebuild. The script reads `Player.lineId IS NOT NULL` rows, computes the canonical mapping via the same slug-stripping helper as the JWT path, and SETs each entry into Redis with the 24h TTL. Idempotent — safe to re-run. Per-row decisions: CREATE (Redis missing), MATCH (Redis = Prisma), DRIFT-OVERWRITE (Redis ≠ Prisma; Prisma wins). Pure decision helper in `decideBackfillAction` is unit-tested.

### State-based data on Redis (v1.5.0 architectural pattern)

Two stores in this codebase follow a shared shape: Redis is the canonical read source, Prisma is the durable secondary. Player mapping (PR 16 / v1.5.0) was the first; RSVP (PR 19 / v1.7.0) is the second. New stores added under this pattern should match these nine principles so the operational story stays uniform.

1. **Redis is canonical for the read path.** The hot read goes Redis-direct. No `unstable_cache` wrapper on top of Redis (the cache TTL would just be a second layer of staleness on top of an already-fast store).
2. **Prisma is the durable backup.** Same data is persisted to Postgres in the same write — failure of either propagates as an error to the user, partial-write states do not survive. Prisma exists for two reasons: (a) the recovery script reads from it to rebuild Redis on data loss, (b) admin queries that join across many domains (e.g. "show all linked players + their last login") use Prisma where Redis would be a poor index shape.
3. **Tri-state read result.** `{ status: 'hit' | 'miss' | 'error' }` discriminated union, so the caller can apply different policies per branch. Pre-v1.5.0 code collapsed miss/error into a single nullish return and made the policies indistinguishable; never repeat that.
4. **Miss policy is per-domain.** Player mapping: miss returns `null` (orphan; no Prisma fallback in the happy path). RSVP: miss falls through to Prisma + writes back to Redis (cold-cache fill). The choice depends on whether "missing in Redis" is a normal steady state (player mapping: yes — orphan users exist) or always an anomaly (RSVP: a GameWeek not yet seeded should self-heal).
5. **Error policy is universal-defensive.** Any `error` (Upstash unreachable / unconfigured / hgetall threw) falls through to Prisma so a transient outage doesn't break authenticated sessions or null out the dashboard. **Error reads do NOT trigger a write-back** — don't amplify a half-broken connection into a write storm.
6. **TTL is per-domain.** Player mapping uses a sliding 24h TTL (every read fires a fire-and-forget `expire` so active users never expire). RSVP uses an absolute TTL anchored at `max(matchday, now()) + 90 days` — RSVP data has a natural lifetime tied to a real-world event.
7. **Per-write Redis pre-warm.** Every write site that mutates the canonical state does Prisma-first-then-Redis in the same try block. Forgetting the Redis write would leave the store stale until the natural TTL pulls the entry back to a fresh fall-through; load-bearing for read-your-own-writes consistency.
8. **One backfill script per store.** `scripts/backfillRedis<X>FromPrisma.ts`, `--dry-run` / `--apply` modes, idempotent, per-row CREATE/MATCH/DRIFT-OVERWRITE decisions, pure `decideBackfillAction` exported for unit testing. Run dry-run against prod BEFORE merging the no-fallback code so the cutover doesn't trigger a transient cold-Postgres storm.
9. **Tests pin the policy seam.** Each store ships with a Vitest suite that exercises hit/miss/error branches independently, namespace isolation, and the `RedisLike` injection seam. The test seam is `__setRedisClientForTesting(client | null)` — production code never calls it.
10. **Public-write hot paths invert: Redis sync, Prisma deferred via `waitUntil`** (PR 20 / v1.8.0). Public-facing write sites (`/api/assign-player`, `/api/rsvp`) write Redis on the response critical path and defer the durable Prisma write to background via `waitUntil` from `@vercel/functions`. The Redis write is the gate (canonical store consulted by reads); the Prisma write is recoverable on failure via the audit script. Admin write sites stay Prisma-first because admin pages re-read Prisma directly on `revalidatePath('/admin/...')` — deferring there would surface stale state on the admin's own next render. **Throwing variants required.** Public hot paths use `setMappingOrThrow` / `setRsvpOrThrow` (the throwing variants); the silent `setMapping` / `setRsvp` would 200-OK with no durable write landing anywhere on Redis failure (since Prisma is now deferred). No-client (KV env unset) remains silent — that's a dev-only condition. **Drift on background-Prisma failure recovers via two layers.** Inline `console.error('[v1.8.0 DRIFT] kind=<domain> ...')` log lines emit per-failure for operator grep + replay; the per-domain backfill script (`backfillRedis<X>FromPrisma`) covers Redis-side drift (read-side); a new audit script (`auditRedisVsPrisma.ts`) covers the inverse direction (write-side, `--repair-prisma` flag).

11. **Writes to Redis-canonical state should NOT invalidate the static `public-data` cache** (PR 21 / v1.8.2). State that lives in Redis (player mapping, RSVP) is its own read path — `getMapping` / `getRsvpForGameWeeks` are called at session-aware boundaries (JWT callback, dashboard render), NOT through `unstable_cache`. The static `public-data:db` / `public-data:sheets` cache holds team / player / matchday / match / goal / rating data — none of which depend on the link state of any session or the RSVP signals of any player. Calling `revalidatePath('/')` + `revalidateTag('public-data', { expire: 0 })` on a Redis-canonical write therefore forces a needless full re-derivation of the entire `LeagueData` blob (Prisma + RSVP fanout) on the user's next dashboard render — measurably ~580ms warm and multi-second cold per write. The cache-bust shape is reserved for writes that mutate the static fields themselves (admin actions on Team / Player / Match / Goal / Venue, picture-mirror Blob URL updates) and runs from those write sites, not from public hot paths. Concretely: `/api/rsvp` (v1.7.0) and `/api/assign-player` (v1.8.2) drop `revalidatePath('/')` and `revalidateTag('public-data')` from their synchronous response paths. The picture-mirror `uploadAndPersistLinePic` waitUntil keeps its `revalidateTag('public-data', { expire: 0 })` because it does mutate a static field (`Player.pictureUrl`), and that bust runs in the background after the response has already returned. **Audit before adding a `revalidateTag('public-data')` to any new write site:** if the field being written is reachable from `dbToPublicLeagueData` / the `getFromDb` Prisma include, the bust is correct; if not, drop it.

**Stores under this pattern:**

| Store | File | Namespace | TTL | Backfill script |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Player mapping | `src/lib/playerMappingStore.ts` | `t9l:auth:map:` | 24h sliding | `scripts/backfillRedisFromPrisma.ts` |
| RSVP per GameWeek | `src/lib/rsvpStore.ts` | `t9l:rsvp:gw:` | matchday + 90d (absolute) | `scripts/backfillRedisRsvpFromPrisma.ts` |

**Stores explicitly NOT under this pattern (considered and decided against):**

- **Goals / scores** — admin-write-only, not on the public read hot path; the existing `unstable_cache(getFromDb, 30s)` is fine. Match scores change on a human timescale, not a per-request timescale.
- **Profile pics (Vercel Blob URLs)** — already cached in Redis as a value (not a structured store), populated as a side-effect of `assign-player`. The lookup is by player slug and never falls through anywhere — no need for the tri-state policy.
- **Settings (`Setting` table)** — admin-flip cadence is once-a-week or rarer; the `unstable_cache(getDataSource, 30s)` wrapper is sufficient and the cache-bust path on flip is well-covered.
- **LineLogin** — write-only from the JWT callback for admin Flow B; never read on the public hot path.

When in doubt about whether a new domain belongs in Redis-canonical: if the read frequency is **public dashboard render** (every page view, every authenticated user) AND the data has natural cardinality bounded per league/event/user (not unbounded relations), the Redis-canonical pattern fits. Otherwise the `unstable_cache` shape is simpler and adequate.

### Subdomain Routing

`page.tsx` reads the `host` request header and resolves the active league via [`getLeagueIdFromRequest()`](src/lib/getLeagueFromHost.ts) (apex/dev/localhost → default league; known subdomain → that league; unknown subdomain → `null`). The resolved id is passed to `getPublicLeagueData(leagueId)` and the same `Dashboard` renders for both apex and subdomain (v1.25.0 — pre-v1.25.0 a separate `LeaguePublicView` rendered for subdomains).

- `lib/admin-data.ts#getLeagueBySubdomain(subdomain)` — cached Prisma query (revalidate=60, tag=leagues)
- Known non-league hostnames skipped: `www`, `dev`, `localhost`, `t9l`, `127`, empty
- v1.25.0 — `Dashboard` is the single public renderer; the prior subdomain-only `LeaguePublicView` 3-tab view is gone. Subdomain users get RSVP + next-matchday + UserTeamBadge + per-team availability via the same component the apex uses.

## Time handling

T9L is a Tokyo-based football league. Every match kickoff, matchday date, and RSVP deadline displayed to a player or entered by an admin is **JST clock time** (Asia/Tokyo, UTC+9, no DST). Postgres stores `DateTime` columns as UTC instants (TIMESTAMPTZ); the bridge between "UTC instant in DB" and "JST clock time on screen / in form" is the only thing the canonical helpers in [`src/lib/jst.ts`](src/lib/jst.ts) do.

**The V8 / Vercel TZ=UTC trap (the bug v1.9.0 / PR A fixed).** On Vercel, the Node.js process runs with `process.env.TZ` defaulting to UTC. That makes `new Date("2026-04-16T14:30")` in a server action parse the string as UTC clock time — per the ECMAScript spec for ISO-without-Z forms, V8 uses the host TZ; on Vercel that's UTC. So an admin in JST who types "14:30" into the admin schedule editor used to have their submission interpreted as 14:30 UTC = 23:30 JST — a 9-hour skew on every match scheduled by any non-JST admin (and silently hitting JST admins too because the round-trip through the DB then displays back as 23:30 in `Date#getHours()` browser-local rendering, which then made it look "right" to a JST viewer in the input form even though the stored value was wrong).

**Browser `<input type="datetime-local">`** is the same trap from the other end: the input value is the user's *local* clock time as a tz-naive string, so the server cannot infer the user's timezone from the wire format alone. Convention enforced by `lib/jst.ts`: every `<input type="datetime-local">` value (rendered + parsed) represents JST clock time, regardless of the browser's local TZ.

### Convention

1. **Every `<input type="datetime-local">` value (rendered + parsed) represents JST clock time** regardless of browser local TZ. Use `formatJstDateTimeLocal(date)` to populate the input and `parseJstDateTimeLocal(string)` on the server to interpret submissions.
2. **Every `<input type="date">` value is a JST calendar date** stored as UTC midnight (`Date.UTC(y, m, d)`). Helper: `parseJstDateOnly(string)` for the server, `formatJstDate(date)` for the client.
3. **Every display string of a date/time goes through one of the `formatJst*` helpers** in `lib/jst.ts` — never through bare `toLocaleString` / `toLocaleDateString` / `toLocaleTimeString` without an explicit `timeZone: 'Asia/Tokyo'`.
4. **Avoid `Date#getHours()` / `getMinutes()` / `getDate()`** in component code — these read the host's local TZ, not JST. Use `formatJstTime(date)` etc.
5. **Avoid `toISOString().slice(0, 16)` to populate datetime-local inputs** — that's UTC clock time, not JST. Use `formatJstDateTimeLocal(date)`.

### Canonical helpers (from `lib/jst.ts`)

| Helper | Purpose |
|---|---|
| `formatJstDate(d)` | "YYYY-MM-DD" in JST. For `<input type="date">` values + display. |
| `formatJstTime(d)` | "HH:MM" 24h in JST. For display + `<input type="time">` values. |
| `formatJstDateTimeLocal(d)` | "YYYY-MM-DDTHH:mm" in JST. For `<input type="datetime-local">` values. |
| `formatJstFriendly(d, locale)` | "Apr 16 (Thu)" or "4月16日（木）" — replaces `formatMatchDate`. |
| `formatJstShort(d)` | "Sat 16 Apr" admin dashboard short date. |
| `formatJstDayMonth(d)` | "16 Apr" no weekday. |
| `parseJstDateTimeLocal(s)` | Inverse of `formatJstDateTimeLocal`. The load-bearing parser — server actions must use this for `playedAt` / `endedAt`. |
| `parseJstDateOnly(s)` | "YYYY-MM-DD" → UTC midnight Date. |
| `combineJstDateAndTime(date, time)` | "YYYY-MM-DD" + "HH:MM" → UTC Date. |
| `jstIsoString(date, time)` | "YYYY-MM-DDTHH:MM:00+09:00" for use with countdown timers etc. |

### Existing-rows-may-be-skewed risk

Pre-v1.9.0, any admin not in JST (or any admin in JST who used the "Add Match" form when the picker incorrectly displayed UTC) may have produced `Match.playedAt` rows that are 9 hours off — stored as 14:30 UTC instead of 14:30 JST. v1.9.0 stops the bleeding (new edits land correctly), but does NOT bulk-fix existing skewed rows. **Operator action after v1.9.0 deploy:** spot-check `Match.playedAt` rows and re-save any that look wrong via the admin UI (which now displays JST correctly). Bulk-fix scripts are out of scope here because we can't programmatically distinguish "stored correctly as JST 14:30" from "stored skewed as UTC 14:30 (= JST 23:30)" without external context.

### Internationalization (i18n)

i18n is currently delivered via Google Translate's `googtrans` cookie set by [`src/components/LanguageToggle.tsx`](src/components/LanguageToggle.tsx) — there's no custom translation pipeline despite older CLAUDE.md descriptions of `I18nProvider` / `useT()`. The `formatJstFriendly` helper accepts a `'en' | 'ja'` locale parameter so it can render "4月16日（木）" when the caller knows the locale; client components currently default to `'en'`. The Anthropic-translation pipeline described in earlier ledger entries is not present in the current code; ignore.

## Data Source

All data is read from a single Google Sheet via the Sheets API using a service account.

- Sheet ID: `1BLTV9v518fEi3DXRA-qcYY3bLDm_qftNoY_5SNzjKSc`
- Caching: ISR with `revalidate = 300` (5 minutes)
- Read strategy: Single `batchGet` call fetching all 7 tabs per page render
- Write: `writeRosterAvailability()` in `sheets.ts` writes RSVP status back to `RosterRaw` (requires service account Editor access)

### Environment Variables

```
# Google Sheets (service account — needs Editor access for RSVP write-back)
GOOGLE_SERVICE_ACCOUNT_EMAIL
GOOGLE_PRIVATE_KEY             # PEM format, newlines as \n

GOOGLE_SHEET_ID                # 1BLTV9v518fEi3DXRA-qcYY3bLDm_qftNoY_5SNzjKSc

# LINE OAuth (next-auth)
LINE_CLIENT_ID
LINE_CLIENT_SECRET
NEXTAUTH_SECRET
NEXTAUTH_URL                   # https://t9l.me in prod, http://localhost:3000 in dev

# Upstash Redis — canonical store for lineId→Player mapping (v1.5.0) and
# per-GameWeek RSVP signals (v1.7.0). Also caches player-pic Blob URLs.
KV_REST_API_URL
KV_REST_API_TOKEN

# Vercel Blob (player profile pictures — LINE-CDN mirror)
BLOB_READ_WRITE_TOKEN

# Postgres (Neon-Vercel marketplace integration provisions both per branch)
DATABASE_URL                   # Pooled connection (PgBouncer)
DATABASE_URL_UNPOOLED          # Direct connection (used by `prisma migrate deploy` + Prisma `directUrl`)
```

If `GOOGLE_SHEET_ID` or `GOOGLE_SERVICE_ACCOUNT_EMAIL` are absent, `fetchSheetData()` falls back to `lib/mock-data.ts` automatically. Auth features (RSVP, player assignment) degrade gracefully when KV/Blob vars are missing.

### Sheet Tabs & Ranges

| Tab | Range | Purpose |
|-----|-------|---------|
| `TeamRaw` | `A:B` | Team names and logos |
| `RosterRaw` | `A:L` | Players: picture, name, team, position, MD1–MD8 availability (`Y` / `EXPECTED` / `PLAYED` / blank) |
| `ScheduleRaw` | `A:F` | 24 matches: matchday, match number, kickoff, full time, home team, away team |
| `GoalsRaw` | `A:F` | Goals: matchday, timestamp, scoring team, conceding team, scorer, assister |
| `RatingsRaw` | `A:BH` | Peer ratings: matchday, timestamp, respondent team, 53 player columns (1–5), 4 meta columns |
| `Schedule Formula` | `A:E` | Rotation: which team plays first/last/middle/sits out per matchday |
| `MDScheduleRaw` | `A:B` | Matchday dates (label → YYYY-MM-DD or other parseable format) |

### Data Parsing Rules

**Row 1 of every tab is the header row. Skip it.**

**Team name normalization** — RatingsRaw prepends color names. Strip them:
- "Blue Mariners FC" → "Mariners FC"
- "Yellow Fenix FC" → "Fenix FC"
- "Hygge SC" / "FC Torpedo" — no change

**Player ID** — `slugify(name)`: lowercase, strip accents (NFD), replace spaces with `-`, remove non-alphanumeric. Example: "Ian Noseda" → `ian-noseda`.

**Team ID** — same slug approach: "Mariners FC" → `mariners-fc`.

**`#REF!` handling** — GoalsRaw and RatingsRaw column 0 may contain `#REF!`. If value matches `/MD\d+/i`, use it. Otherwise fall back to inferring matchday from timestamp date against `MDScheduleRaw` dates.

**Availability statuses** — `RosterRaw` MD columns: `Y` / `GOING` = confirmed, `EXPECTED` / `UNDECIDED` = tentative, `PLAYED` = actually played, blank = not going. Both confirmed and tentative statuses count toward `availability`. Only `PLAYED` counts toward `played` (used for match stats). New RSVPs write `GOING` / `UNDECIDED` / `''`; legacy `Y` / `EXPECTED` values from the sheet are still parsed correctly.

**Goal-to-match mapping** — Match by `(scoringTeamId, concedingTeamId)` or `(concedingTeamId, scoringTeamId)` within the matchday's 3 matches.

**"Guest" scorer** — non-rostered player, keep as-is in data, exclude from player stat aggregations.

**Ratings** — RatingsRaw is wide. Columns 3 to `header.length - 4` are player columns (header = player name). Last 4 columns are meta ratings: refereeing, gamesClose, teamwork, enjoyment.

## File Structure

```
src/
├── app/
│   ├── layout.tsx                    # RootLayout: AuthProvider, ThemeProvider, Sonner Toaster (PR 17 / v1.6.0 — global toast surface that survives route navigation)
│   ├── page.tsx                      # Server component: resolves leagueId via getLeagueIdFromRequest, fetches via publicData, renders Dashboard (v1.25.0 — apex + subdomain unified)
│   ├── globals.css                   # Tailwind + custom design tokens
│   ├── admin/                        # Admin shell (Credentials provider) — settings, players, schedule, etc.
│   ├── assign-player/page.tsx        # Player-link picker (Server) → AssignPlayerClient
│   ├── auth-error/, dev-login/       # Auth error UI + dev-only login bypass
│   ├── schedule/, stats/             # Public sub-routes
│   └── api/
│       ├── auth/[...nextauth]/       # next-auth handler
│       ├── assign-player/route.ts    # POST/DELETE: link/unlink lineId → playerId. Redis-canonical (v1.8.0); Prisma deferred via waitUntil.
│       └── rsvp/route.ts             # POST: link RSVP. Redis-canonical (v1.7.0); Prisma deferred (v1.8.0).
├── components/
│   ├── Dashboard.tsx                 # Client: 3-tab home (default-league public view from Sheets/DB)
│   ├── NextMatchdayBanner.tsx        # Match cards above the fold
│   ├── MatchdayAvailability.tsx      # Per-team attendance pitch view
│   ├── LeagueTable.tsx, TopPerformers.tsx, SquadList.tsx, MatchdayCard.tsx, …
│   ├── LanguageToggle.tsx            # EN/JP switch (sets `googtrans` cookie; Google Translate)
│   ├── PlayerAvatar.tsx              # Avatar with fallback chain (LINE CDN → /player_pics/{slug}.png → default)
│   ├── RsvpBar.tsx, RsvpButton.tsx   # In-Dashboard RSVP UX
│   ├── LineLoginButton.tsx, GuestLoginBanner.tsx
│   ├── AssignPlayerClient.tsx        # /assign-player client form
│   ├── UserTeamBadge.tsx             # "Your team is X" pill (v1.11.0)
│   ├── VersionFooter.tsx             # Renders APP_VERSION
│   ├── ThemeProvider.tsx, ThemeToggle.tsx
│   └── admin/, ui/                   # Admin tabs + shadcn-style primitives
├── lib/
│   ├── ids.ts                        # Shared "p-"/"t-" prefix constants + slug↔DB-id helpers (v1.12)
│   ├── sheets.ts                     # batchGet (read) + writeRosterAvailability (write)
│   ├── data.ts                       # parseTeams/parsePlayers/parseSchedule/parseGoals/parseRatings
│   ├── stats.ts                      # computeLeagueTable/computePlayerStats/findNextMatchday
│   ├── jst.ts                        # Canonical JST date/time helpers (v1.9.0)
│   ├── auth.ts                       # next-auth authOptions (LINE provider, JWT, Redis-primary lookup)
│   ├── playerMappingStore.ts         # Upstash-canonical store for lineId→Player (v1.5.0) — 24h sliding TTL, tri-state get
│   ├── rsvpStore.ts                  # Upstash-canonical store for per-GameWeek RSVP (v1.7.0) — HASH per GW, absolute TTL = matchday + 90d
│   ├── rsvpStoreSchema.ts            # Pure schema constants (key prefix, sentinel, TTL) shared with backfillRedisRsvpFromPrisma (v1.12)
│   ├── rsvpMerge.ts                  # Pure helpers — mapAvailability + mergeRsvpData merge Redis RSVP into LeagueData
│   ├── publicData.ts                 # Dispatcher: cached static read + uncached RSVP read merged into LeagueData
│   ├── dbToPublicLeagueData.ts       # Prisma → LeagueData adapter (static fields only post-v1.7.0)
│   ├── settings.ts                   # `dataSource` / `writeMode` Setting helpers (resolveDataSource defaults to 'db' since v1.12)
│   ├── linkedPlayers.ts              # /assign-player picker: Prisma `Player.lineId` fetch — filters already-linked
│   ├── optimisticLink.ts, assignSubmit.ts, assignToast.ts, assignButtonLabel.ts  # /assign-player UX helpers
│   ├── userTeam.ts                   # pickUserTeam helper for UserTeamBadge (v1.11.0)
│   ├── admin-data.ts                 # Cached Prisma queries for admin tabs + getOrphanLineLogins
│   ├── revalidate.ts                 # revalidatePublicData() — bust public-data cache after admin writes
│   ├── getLeagueFromHost.ts          # Subdomain extraction for app/page.tsx
│   ├── prisma.ts                     # Prisma client singleton
│   ├── version.ts                    # APP_VERSION single-source constant
│   └── mock-data.ts                  # Fallback data when Sheets credentials absent
└── types/
    └── index.ts                      # All TypeScript interfaces
```

### Internationalization

i18n is delivered via Google Translate's `googtrans` cookie set by [`src/components/LanguageToggle.tsx`](src/components/LanguageToggle.tsx). Despite older ledger entries, there is no custom translation pipeline (`I18nProvider` / `useT()` / Anthropic translate cache). The `formatJstFriendly` helper accepts a `'en' | 'ja'` locale parameter so server-side date rendering can match the page language; client components currently default to `'en'`.

## Commands

```bash
npm run dev          # Local dev (uses mock data if env vars absent)
npm run build        # Production build
npm run lint         # ESLint
```

## Important Notes

- **4 teams, ~53 players, 8 matchdays, 24 matches**, 33-minute match duration
- FC Torpedo players have no positions in the sheet — store as `null`, display "—"
- Matchday dates come from `MDScheduleRaw`, not `ScheduleRaw`. Display "TBD" when null.
- `computeMatchScores`: if a matchday has any goals at all, all 3 matches are treated as played (even if 0-0). This is a simplification — no explicit "match finished" flag exists.
- Player pictures: `/stats` reads Redis `player-pic:<slug>` → Vercel Blob URL (mirror of the LINE display picture, written by `/api/assign-player`'s background `uploadAndPersistLinePic`). Other public surfaces use `PlayerAvatar`'s static fallback chain (LINE CDN URL → `/player_pics/{slug}.png` → `default.png`).
- The `/minato` route redirects to the team's AppSheet data-entry form

## Prisma schema (admin-side / DB cutover target)

`prisma/schema.prisma` defines the DB-backed admin and (post-cutover) public-site source of truth. Key models:

- **`User`** — admin/viewer accounts (`role: ADMIN|VIEWER`). LINE-linked via `lineId @unique`.
- **`League`** — single league instance (e.g. "T9L 2026 Spring"). Has `subdomain @unique` for subdomain-based public routing. **Restored fields** `isDefault Boolean`, `primaryColor String?`, `accentColor String?` were re-added to the schema in PR 1 to match prod's actual columns; they're orphan from a rolled-back per-league-branding feature, populated only on `T9L 2026 Spring` (`isDefault: true`) and `Test League 2025` (`isDefault: false`). No code reads them today.
- **`Team`** + **`LeagueTeam`** — teams are global brand identities (`Team`); a team's participation in a league is `LeagueTeam`. PR 1 added `Team.shortName String?` and `Team.color String?`. `Team.name` is **not `@unique`** because the test-league seed introduced duplicates (`Storm United`, `Phoenix FC`); upserts key on `id` (slug) instead.
- **`Player`** + **`PlayerLeagueAssignment`** — players are global; league participation is recorded with `fromGameWeek` / `toGameWeek`. PR 1 added `Player.position String?` (FC Torpedo players are intentionally null).
- **`Venue`** — PR 1 added `url String?`, `courtSize String?`, and `name @unique`.
- **`GameWeek`** — `(leagueId, weekNumber) @@unique`. Has optional `venueId`.
- **`Match`** — PR 1 added `@@unique([gameWeekId, homeTeamId, awayTeamId])` so the upcoming backfill can `prisma.match.upsert` by natural key. Constraint is safe under T9L's 4-team round-robin (each pair plays once per MD); revisit if format ever allows the same pair to play twice in one MD.
- **`Goal`** + **`Assist`** — `Goal` cascades on `Match` delete; **does not cascade on `Player` delete** (deleting a Player with goals will FK-fail — admin "remove from league" only deletes `PlayerLeagueAssignment`, not `Player`).
- **`Availability`** *(new in PR 1)* — RSVP per `(playerId, gameWeekId) @@unique`. Two enums: `RsvpStatus { GOING, UNDECIDED, NOT_GOING }` and `ParticipatedStatus { JOINED, NO_SHOWED }`. Cascades on Player and GameWeek delete. Public-site RSVP route will dual-write to this table starting PR 3.
- **`Setting`** *(new in PR 1)* — `(category, key, leagueId) @@unique` composite. `leagueId IS NULL` rows are global; per-league rows override. Used by upcoming PR 3 to store `(public, dataSource) ∈ {sheets, db}` and `(public, writeMode) ∈ {sheets-only, dual, db-only}` toggles. Cascades on League delete.
- **`LineLogin`** *(new in PR 6)* — Tracks every distinct LINE user that has authenticated against the public site, regardless of whether they've been linked to a Player record. Upserted from `lib/auth.ts#trackLineLogin` on every JWT callback that has a `lineId`. `lineId @unique` plus `@@index([lastSeenAt])` for sorted-by-recency orphan queries. Drives the admin "Assign Player" Flow B dropdown — orphan = `LineLogin` row whose `lineId` is not currently set on any `Player.lineId`. Powers `lib/admin-data.ts#getOrphanLineLogins()`.

The `directUrl` connection in `datasource db { ... }` reads from `DATABASE_URL_UNPOOLED` (matches the Neon-Vercel integration's canonical var name). The legacy `DIRECT_URL` var is also still set on production and Preview (dev) for backwards compatibility but no longer referenced by the schema.

## Testing

Two tools, both wired into `package.json` and CI.

| Stack | Purpose | Where |
|---|---|---|
| **Vitest** | Pure-function and module-level tests; run in CI on every PR | `tests/unit/**/*.test.ts(x)`; config in `vitest.config.ts` |
| **Playwright** | End-to-end tests against a base URL (defaults to `https://t9l.me`); run locally pre-merge for PR 3+ user-flow changes | `tests/e2e/**/*.spec.ts`; config in `playwright.config.ts`; override base URL with `BASE_URL=https://<preview>.vercel.app npm run test:e2e` |

Scripts:

```bash
npm test            # vitest watch
npm run test:run    # vitest one-shot (same as CI)
npm run test:e2e    # playwright against $BASE_URL (default https://t9l.me)
npm run test:ci     # vitest only (e2e is opt-in in CI for now)
```

CI workflow `.github/workflows/test.yml` runs `npm ci`, `prisma generate` (placeholder URLs — no DB connection needed for codegen), `tsc --noEmit`, then `vitest run`. PRs are merge-blocked on red.

What to add per change-type:

- **Pure-function or library change** (e.g. `lib/data.ts`, `lib/stats.ts`, parsers, mappers) → Vitest unit test with explicit input/output. Example: `tests/unit/slugify.test.ts`.
- **API route or server action change** → Vitest test that calls the handler directly (mock `next-auth` session if auth-gated); assert response status + body shape.
- **Public UI flow change** (anything visible at apex `/`, `/schedule`, `/stats`, `/admin`) → Playwright e2e covering the user-visible behavior. Run against the PR's preview URL (`BASE_URL=<preview>`) before requesting merge.
- **Backfill / migration script change** → Vitest unit tests for row mappers (Sheets row → Prisma create input). Integration test that runs the full backfill against the per-PR Neon branch DB and asserts row counts + spot-check fields.
- **Schema change** → No new test required for the migration itself (Prisma's `migrate deploy` covers correctness), but any code that reads new fields needs a unit or e2e test.

## Backups & rollback runbook

Every PR that ships ≥ PR 2 has four parallel rollback paths. Sequencing of *which* path to invoke depends on what broke.

### Layer 1 — Git tag reset (fastest if the bad change is the latest commit on `main`)
- Each PR's merge commit is tagged `v-pre-pr-<N+1>-<slug>` (e.g. `v-pre-pr-2-backfill` is the last-known-good before PR 2 merges).
- To revert main locally: `git fetch origin --tags && git reset --hard v-pre-pr-2-backfill`. **Do not push --force to main** — instead create a revert PR: `git revert <merge-sha>` and merge that.
- Tags are immutable; check listing with `git tag -l "v-pre-pr-*" -n1`.

### Layer 2 — Vercel deploy promotion (fastest if you need prod restored without waiting for CI)
- Vercel retains every prior production deploy. Each PR's "last good prod deploy URL" is recorded in this section as it lands.
- To promote a previous prod deploy back to current: `vercel promote <deploy-url>` (e.g. `vercel promote https://t9l-website-784a0vmrz-t9l-app.vercel.app`).
- This rolls back code + the running build only. Schema/data are unaffected — pair with Layer 3 if the issue was DB-side.

### Layer 3 — Neon branch restore (when the DB itself is wrong)
- Before each PR ≥ 2 merges, a snapshot Neon branch is cut from `production`: `neonctl branches create --name pre-pr-<N>-<slug> --parent production --project-id young-lake-57212861`. This captures the DB state pre-PR.
- To restore prod to the snapshot state: `neonctl branches restore production --source pre-pr-<N>-<slug> --project-id young-lake-57212861`. This is destructive on the current `production` branch — confirm with the operator before invoking.
- The connection URI for a snapshot branch (read-only inspection) is fetchable via `neonctl connection-string <branch-id> --project-id young-lake-57212861`.
- Project ID: `young-lake-57212861`. Default branch on Neon is named `production` (not `main`). Org: `org-floral-feather-76166317`.

### Layer 4 — Sheets snapshot (when public-site Sheets data needs reverting)
- Before PR 2 (the first PR after which dual-write or backfill could touch any data adjacent to Sheets), make a date-stamped duplicate of the source spreadsheet via Drive: File → Make a copy → name `T9L Roster Snapshot YYYY-MM-DD pre-pr-N`. Record the snapshot file ID below.
- Restore by copying values back from the snapshot to the live sheet (same tabs, same ranges).
- Source Sheet ID: `1BLTV9v518fEi3DXRA-qcYY3bLDm_qftNoY_5SNzjKSc`. Snapshots: *(none yet — PR 1 didn't touch Sheets; first snapshot will be cut before PR 2 merges).*

### Layer 5 — Redis player-mapping store rebuild (PR 16 / v1.5.0)
- The lineId→Player auth lookup is now Redis-canonical (`src/lib/playerMappingStore.ts`, namespace `t9l:auth:map:`, 24h sliding TTL). If Upstash ever loses data — accidental wipe, namespace cleared, region failover with stale state, etc. — every authenticated session degrades to "orphan" until the store is rebuilt. Prisma `Player.lineId` is the durable secondary that the rebuild reads from.
- Recovery procedure: pull the prod env into the local shell so `KV_REST_API_URL`, `KV_REST_API_TOKEN`, and `DATABASE_URL` point at production, then run:
  ```
  npx tsx scripts/backfillRedisFromPrisma.ts --dry-run --verbose   # plan
  npx tsx scripts/backfillRedisFromPrisma.ts --apply --verbose     # execute
  ```
  The script is idempotent — safe to run repeatedly. Per-row decisions are CREATE (Redis missing the entry), MATCH (Redis = Prisma), DRIFT-OVERWRITE (Redis ≠ Prisma; Prisma wins on rebuild). The dry-run mode reports counts + drift detail; review before applying. Apply takes ~1 second per Player row at typical roster size (~30 entries).
- The auth callback's defensive Prisma fallback (`error: redis-error` branch in `getPlayerMapping`) keeps existing JWTs working through a transient Upstash blip — but a sustained outage where the cache is intact-but-different (e.g. someone manually wrote bad keys) would still serve incorrect data. Rebuild from Prisma when in doubt.

### Layer 5b — Redis RSVP store rebuild (PR 19 / v1.7.0)

- The per-GameWeek RSVP read path is now Redis-canonical (`src/lib/rsvpStore.ts`, namespace `t9l:rsvp:gw:`, absolute TTL = matchday + 90 days). If Upstash ever loses data — accidental wipe, namespace cleared, region failover — the public dashboard would render with empty availability for affected GameWeeks until the publicData backfill self-heals on the next render (Prisma fallback + write-back). The recovery script forces a full eager rebuild instead of waiting on per-render self-heal.
- Recovery procedure: pull the prod env into the local shell so `KV_REST_API_URL`, `KV_REST_API_TOKEN`, and `DATABASE_URL` point at production, then run:
  ```
  npx tsx scripts/backfillRedisRsvpFromPrisma.ts --dry-run --verbose   # plan
  npx tsx scripts/backfillRedisRsvpFromPrisma.ts --apply --verbose     # execute
  ```
  The script is idempotent — safe to run repeatedly. Per-GameWeek decisions: CREATE (Redis hash absent), MATCH (Redis = Prisma), DRIFT-OVERWRITE (Redis ≠ Prisma; Prisma wins on rebuild — DELs the existing hash first to ensure onlyInRedis fields don't survive). The dry-run reports counts + per-GW field-level diff (`onlyInPrisma` / `onlyInRedis` / `differing`); review before applying. Pure decision helper `decideBackfillAction` is unit-tested in `tests/unit/backfillRedisRsvpFromPrisma.test.ts`.
- Cutover protocol (mandatory at v1.7.0 deploy time): run `--dry-run` against prod Upstash BEFORE merging the v1.7.0 code. All decisions should be CREATE on a fresh prod (Redis namespace empty pre-deploy). After operator review, run `--apply`. Then merge. Reverse order means the first dashboard render post-deploy hits miss for every GW and falls through to Prisma simultaneously — transient cold-Neon storm.

### Layer 5c — Write-side drift recovery: Redis → Prisma audit (PR 20 / v1.8.0)

- v1.8.0 inverts the public-write hot path: `/api/assign-player` POST/DELETE and `/api/rsvp` POST write Redis synchronously and defer the Prisma write via `waitUntil`. If the deferred Prisma write fails (cold-Neon timeout, transient connection issue), the route emits a `[v1.8.0 DRIFT]` log line — but the durable Prisma row is still missing (or stale).
- Layers 5 + 5b cover the OPPOSITE direction (Redis stale, Prisma fresh — the read-side drift case from v1.5.0/v1.7.0). Layer 5c handles write-side drift.
- Recovery procedure: pull prod env into the local shell so `KV_REST_API_URL`, `KV_REST_API_TOKEN`, and `DATABASE_URL` point at production, then run:
  ```
  npx tsx scripts/auditRedisVsPrisma.ts                      # dry-run, both domains
  npx tsx scripts/auditRedisVsPrisma.ts --domain=playerMapping --verbose
  npx tsx scripts/auditRedisVsPrisma.ts --domain=rsvp --verbose
  npx tsx scripts/auditRedisVsPrisma.ts --repair-prisma      # actually repair
  ```
  The script scans `t9l:auth:map:*` and `t9l:rsvp:gw:*` namespaces, compares to Prisma `Player.lineId` and `Availability` rows, and reports per-row state. Categories: MATCH (both align), REDIS-ONLY (v1.8.0 drift — Redis canonical, Prisma missing — repair fixes), PRISMA-ONLY (read-side drift; Layer 5/5b territory, not repaired here), DIFFERING (same row exists on both sides with different values; Redis canonical wins on repair), MALFORMED (admin-garbage Redis values, reported only). Idempotent — safe to re-run. Pure decision helpers are unit-tested in `tests/unit/auditRedisVsPrisma.test.ts`.
- When to run: after a Vercel logs check that surfaces any `[v1.8.0 DRIFT]` log lines. Or as a periodic operator audit (recommended monthly until the v1.8.0 deferred-write path has demonstrated stable durability — the script is read-only by default so a dry-run is cheap).
